  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_03414b09-ffcb-437d-8df6-143424f05064'
      });

  <span id="freeText2941133175220814590" style="display:none"><i>Michael must save his mother—and protect his powers—in the electric sequel to the #1 New York Times bestselling Michael Vey, from Richard Paul Evans.</i><br /><br />Michael was born with special electrical powers—and he’s not the only one. His friend Taylor has them too, and so do other kids around the world. With Michael’s friend Ostin, a tecno-genius, they form the Electroclan, an alliance meant to protect them from a powerful group, the growing Order of Elgen, who are out to destroy them. The leader of the Elgen, Dr. Hatch, has kidnapped Michael’s mother, and time is running out.<br /><br />After narrowly escaping an Elgen trap, Ostin’s discovery of bizarre “rat fires” in South America leads the gang to the jungles of Peru, where the Electroclan meets new, powerful foes and faces their greatest challenge yet as Michael learns the extent of the Elgen’s rise in power—and the truth of their plan to “restructure” the world.</span>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27179072-drewthereader20?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1611758745&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1611758745" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7581014054910891335">Michael Vey 2: Rise of the Elgen By Richard Paul Evans<br/>	Michael Vey Rise of the Elgen is a second book to the Michael Vey series written by Richard Paul Evans! This is a second book in a series and the first one is called: Michael Vey: The Prisoner of Cell 25.<br/>	In the first book we find out that our main character Michael is the only kid in the family! And, so he lives with his mother. We also find out that he has these superpowers that when he wants too he can eltcuate them! During, the first nov</span>
  <span id="freeText7581014054910891335" style="display:none">Michael Vey 2: Rise of the Elgen By Richard Paul Evans<br />	Michael Vey Rise of the Elgen is a second book to the Michael Vey series written by Richard Paul Evans! This is a second book in a series and the first one is called: Michael Vey: The Prisoner of Cell 25.<br />	In the first book we find out that our main character Michael is the only kid in the family! And, so he lives with his mother. We also find out that he has these superpowers that when he wants too he can eltcuate them! During, the first novel he turns thirteen. And, he got a watch as a present from his Mom because it used to belong to his Dad. Which we also find out that his Dad somehow tragically died when he was five years old. Then, Michael his Mom, and Ostin, his best friend all went out to dinner together to celebrate his big thirteenth birthday. As they were getting done with dinner they walk out and a gunman is standing outside the door waiting for them. Because, he knows about Michael’s power and also because Taylor who is a cheerleader at school helps him because they have the same power. So Taylor look up this school they heard of and they got caught. Taylor got kidnap by evil Dr. Hatch. And the gunman worked for Dr. Hatch. So then the gunman kidnap his mother and took her to this academy.<br />	From there on, Michael and Ostin found Taylor and got her free. But, then they had to go on this big quest to find Michael’s mother. And so the quest continues in the second book…<br />	Let’s get to know our characters a little better! Michael: he is our protagonist of the story and leader of the group call: The Electroclan. Then there’s Ostin: which his mother missed spelled his name because they were born in Texas. And it’s spell Austin. Not Ostin. Which I thought was funny! <br /> Anyways… Ostin is our computer geek and Michael’s best and only friend. Well before they meet Taylor.<br />	Taylor is this tall sophomore (Or was a sophomore) blond girl. She’s also the school’s cheerleader. Which quickly caught Michael’s attention. And they are boyfriend and girlfriends.<br />	Anyways, in the second book of this series it left off right where we were in the first book. So you don’t need to re-read the first book before going into this one. The whole gang escapes the Elgen’s academy and so they had to go back to Michael’s house. So they got to Michael’s house and had to make a whole new plan to find Michael’s mother. Because, they have some clues of where she might be!<br />	As they go on they all meet this guy who owns a plane and who hate Dr. Hatch! So, then the person agrees with Michael in helping out to find his mom. This was Michael’s first time flying in an airplane too! As they got to their destination they landed in a rainforest! The whole gang goes on this other big quest to find Michael’s mother.<br />	As they got to where Dr. Hatch’s “Secret hid-out” they see Mrs. Vey with Dr. Hatch! But, of course they can’t just have his mother unless someone stays behind… <br />For me this sequel was a little slow and a little more serious than the first book because the first one was: Getting to know the world and having a grand old time! But this one we already know the world and we know what might happen next.<br />	Overall, I really enjoyed this sequel. It was a little slow like I said before. But, it was really good. Overall rating is a: 4.5/5 stars! I really enjoyed it!<br /><br /><br /><br />September 10, 2017<br />I didn't realize that I have written a full review of this the first time around. I gave it a four out of five stars!(:</span>

<div id="review_547290976" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/547290976" />
    <a title="Kit Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11741277-kit-kat"><img alt="Kit Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466444294p2/11741277.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/547290976?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kit Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kit Kat" href="/user/show/11741277-kit-kat">Kit Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11741277-kit-kat?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11741277-kit-kat?shelf=books-that-isabel-would-like">books-that-isabel-would-like</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11741277-kit-kat?shelf=books-that-i-will-never-forget">books-that-i-will-never-forget</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11741277-kit-kat?shelf=u-n-b-e-l-i-v-e-a-b-le">u-n-b-e-l-i-v-e-a-b-le</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11741277-kit-kat?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11741277-kit-kat?shelf=wish-it-was-real">wish-it-was-real</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11741277-kit-kat?shelf=writers-united">writers-united</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer547290976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1598085323527360088">I must say I am incredibly glad I saw this on the shelf at a bookstore and decided to read it. The first one was Phenominale and I wish the third one would come out faster. But here's the gist of it. Michael is a very well thought out character who is very out going and brave. The story was a little Cliche but I enjoyed it none the less. It's one of those books you read just to know the good guy would win, get the girl, and save his family. It made me wonder why others gave soooooo much attentio</span>
  <span id="freeText1598085323527360088" style="display:none">I must say I am incredibly glad I saw this on the shelf at a bookstore and decided to read it. The first one was Phenominale and I wish the third one would come out faster. But here's the gist of it. Michael is a very well thought out character who is very out going and brave. The story was a little Cliche but I enjoyed it none the less. It's one of those books you read just to know the good guy would win, get the girl, and save his family. It made me wonder why others gave soooooo much attention to Twilight and Harry Potter when there are amazing gold mines like this just sitting there and do they get all of the Media watching them or interview with the author? No. Yet I would Call this ((and please dont kill me, personal opinion)) better than Harry potter and Twilight. It was a comfort read, one where I knew that everything would turn out all right from the beginning, Yet it kept the pages flying and left me with piles of homework that I push off to the side just so I could read this book. I would recommend it to anyone who like's sic-fi or stuff like that. Until next time, and I doubt anyone reads my review but if you do I'll be back to you soon with my next review<br />Kit kat <br />OUT </span>

<div id="review_396980116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396980116" />
    <a title="Jackie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1159939-jackie"><img alt="Jackie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/396980116?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie" href="/user/show/1159939-jackie">Jackie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer396980116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4064840053734459849">While the writing is ok - mostly fast-paced and definitely held my interest - this one suffered the frequent "sophomore slump". Yes, I understand this is science fiction. Yes, I've read science fiction before. No, science fiction isn't my favorite genre, but I still finished the book.<br/><br/>If I were being nit-picky, which I really try not to, I could list several things that I felt were thrown in just because the author could. They didn't really add to the plot, nor even the enjoyment of reading. They</span>
  <span id="freeText4064840053734459849" style="display:none">While the writing is ok - mostly fast-paced and definitely held my interest - this one suffered the frequent "sophomore slump". Yes, I understand this is science fiction. Yes, I've read science fiction before. No, science fiction isn't my favorite genre, but I still finished the book.<br /><br />If I were being nit-picky, which I really try not to, I could list several things that I felt were thrown in just because the author could. They didn't really add to the plot, nor even the enjoyment of reading. They seemed to be just filler material. But I'm not really in the mood to enumerate those things.<br /><br />Let's just jump to my final thoughts:<br /><br />1. I still think there are too many characters that are just peripheral. It's too hard to keep track of all of them.<br /><br />2. There seemed to be barely disguised mini-sermons. I say this because there were a couple times I thought (while reading) that I was feeling manipulated. I dislike this approach. Mini-sermons are fine if they are overt, or are more thoroughly disguised. <br /><br />3. Even though it is peopled with teenagers, it didn't quite feel like teens were the target audience.<br /><br />4. This one is quite personal: I abhor rats. Making them electric and mob-mentality-ruled (and in massive quantities) bothered me even more. (Nit-picking here - it was clearly stated how high these rats could jump, but when the kids were trying to escape through the tunnels the rats somehow couldn't/didn't jump up and get them? Disconnect for me.) <br /><br />5. I'm not fond of cliff-hanger endings. I like things resolved, wrapped up in paper and tied with a bow. The exception to this is a sequel that is readily and immediately available. By the time the new book comes out, I will have forgotten - or no longer care - what happened to everyone. I really get irritated when things are just left hanging.<br /><br />Final tally - 2 stars. Wish I could do better, but this is, after all, a subjective forum. We'll see what the next installment brings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4064840053734459849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_402952109" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/402952109" />
    <a title="Alisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1095594-alisa"><img alt="Alisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565748842p2/1095594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/402952109?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alisa" href="/user/show/1095594-alisa">Alisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer402952109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5104933850198303141">My two complaints: This book came out on the second day of school... right as I'm trying to get my kids back in school! Even though I had limited time, I squeezed in some time to read this book because I really liked the first book. The second complaint: The cliffhanger that has me waiting another year (and I just heard that this is a 6-book series - Yikes!).<br/><br/>Michael and his friends escape the Elgen, meet an anonymous ally (known as "the Voice") who helps them with one of the escapes and gives th</span>
  <span id="freeText5104933850198303141" style="display:none">My two complaints: This book came out on the second day of school... right as I'm trying to get my kids back in school! Even though I had limited time, I squeezed in some time to read this book because I really liked the first book. The second complaint: The cliffhanger that has me waiting another year (and I just heard that this is a 6-book series - Yikes!).<br /><br />Michael and his friends escape the Elgen, meet an anonymous ally (known as "the Voice") who helps them with one of the escapes and gives them the resources to get to Peru, and penetrate a heavily-guarded fortress in Peru to rescue his mother. It takes the talents of all the electric children, the brains of Ostin, and the brawn of Jack and Wade... plus a few new characters and one more defector to make it all happen!<br /><br />We also learn in this book how evil Dr. Hatch really is... some of those parts were a little disturbing, but necessary to show what Michael Vey and the Electroclan are really up against!<br /><br />I can't wait to read the next book in this series... I only wish it would come out sooner... *sigh*<br /><br />Now to clean my house which has been severely neglected while I read this book and got my kids back in school... ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5104933850198303141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15519266398500386430"><br/> <br/> An excellent book. Made for a great family read-a-loud. One thing to note, Richard Paul Evans promoted this series as one that was supposed to be as action-packed as other popular young adult books such as Harry Potter and Hunger Games, but without being as dark and demented. I would say that the first book of the series lived up to that claim, but this second book exposed much more of the villian in this story and was much darker.   <span id="freeText15519266398500386430" style="display:none"><br /> <br /> An excellent book. Made for a great family read-a-loud. One thing to note, Richard Paul Evans promoted this series as one that was supposed to be as action-packed as other popular young adult books such as Harry Potter and Hunger Games, but without being as dark and demented. I would say that the first book of the series lived up to that claim, but this second book exposed much more of the villian in this story and was much darker. Some of the death scenes were especially gruesome and might be traumatic for a younger reader. While not being as dark and traumatic as say the Hunger Games, I don't think it lives up to the advertizing.<br /><br />False advertizing aside, the book was exciting, fun to read, and hard to put down.<br /><br />The ending is a complete cliff-hanger leaving you frothing at the mount for the next installment of the series.</span>

<div id="review_1979886554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1979886554" />
    <a title="Valliya Rennell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58882300-valliya-rennell"><img alt="Valliya Rennell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596694907p2/58882300.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1979886554?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valliya Rennell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valliya Rennell" href="/user/show/58882300-valliya-rennell">Valliya Rennell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=a-3-5-stars">a-3-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=d-fantasy">d-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=d-science-fiction">d-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=x-reviewed-books">x-reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=d-crime">d-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1979886554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6899566285296560908">3 stars<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/46097.Richard_Paul_Evans' title='Richard Paul Evans' rel='nofollow noopener'>Richard Paul Evans</a> took an interesting turn in the plot of his Michael Vey series in book two: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12988089.Rise_of_the_Elgen__Michael_Vey___2_' title='Rise of the Elgen (Michael Vey, #2) by Richard Paul Evans' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rise of the Elgen</a>. The next book in the series follows Michael and the Electroclan as they escape the Elgen in book one, and later try to find his mother. While trying to locate her the Elgen keeps on attacking and a mysterious voice seems to be watching them.... Or is he? <b>Will Michael succeed in finding his mother <i>and</i> escaping the Elgen?</b><br/><br/>Book two in the Michael Vey franchise was a good book.<b> It </b></span>
  <span id="freeText6899566285296560908" style="display:none">3 stars<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/46097.Richard_Paul_Evans" title="Richard Paul Evans" rel="nofollow noopener">Richard Paul Evans</a> took an interesting turn in the plot of his Michael Vey series in book two: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12988089.Rise_of_the_Elgen__Michael_Vey___2_" title="Rise of the Elgen (Michael Vey, #2) by Richard Paul Evans" rel="nofollow noopener">Rise of the Elgen</a>. The next book in the series follows Michael and the Electroclan as they escape the Elgen in book one, and later try to find his mother. While trying to locate her the Elgen keeps on attacking and a mysterious voice seems to be watching them.... Or is he? <b>Will Michael succeed in finding his mother <i>and</i> escaping the Elgen?</b><br /><br />Book two in the Michael Vey franchise was a good book.<b> It didn't live up to its predecessor</b>, but I can't say that it was a bad book. I would recommend it to people who like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187.The_Lightning_Thief__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___1_" title="The Lightning Thief (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lightning Thief</a> (Percy Jackson) novels. It is another adventure novel with an average written main character, but unfortunately, <b>it didn't bring anything new to the table</b>.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“The man glanced at him, then continued. 'The ants protect the tree and the tree gives them shelter. The ants will attack animals who come too close. They will even kill any plant that tries to grow near it. The natives used to tie their enemies to the tree. The ants would eat them alive.'”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I did appreciate it that there was a use of real world facts. Ostin, Michael's best friend (he isn't a Glow), is some type of the new "Einstein." He constantly comes up with new plans by using logical thinking and real world information, like when he <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[came up with the plan to use the water pipes as a part of their escape plan to bail Michael out of prison, near the end of the novel. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It was really neat how the <b>real world knowledge tied into the fictional ideas also.</b><br /><br />I liked also the <b>development of Zeus.</b> In my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11337912.The_Prisoner_of_Cell_25__Michael_Vey___1_" title="The Prisoner of Cell 25 (Michael Vey, #1) by Richard Paul Evans" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prisoner of Cell 25</a> review, I said that he was a character that was just <i>there.</i> Now, he grew into an awesome part of the team. He is a great fighter and loyal to Michael at all costs. He's grown into a character that can be truly admired.<br /><br /><b>I also mentioned that I disliked Wade and Tara. <br /><br />This didn't change.</b> Though Zeus went through so much character development... I can't say the same about Tara and Wade. First of all, Wade. <b>He was there with the Electroclan, trying to spice up the atmosphere with a few jokes and.... that's about it.</b> He never had a big role in the book. I can almost foresee his death in the next few novels, as it surely will come. Almost as if he was only written to be killed off. I think that in total, he said about 20 lines of dialogue in the WHOLE ENTIRE NOVEL. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Mrs. Vey stared at her for a moment, then breathed out slowly. 'No, he’s not. Your father’s not a schoolteacher, he’s a police officer. And you didn’t give Michael that watch for his birthday. I did.'<br />Tara glanced nervously at Dr. Hatch.<br />'Who are you and why do you look just like Taylor?' Mrs. Vey asked.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Boohoo for Tara.<br /><br />I found her tolerable in book 1 as she had at least a purpose. She and Taylor had a well written love-turned-to-hate sister relationship. In book two, however, <b>she was there to be Taylor's evil twin. </b>She fooled Mrs. Vey into thinking that she was Taylor, though she didn't really succeed. She tried to fool Michael... and didn't succeed. AAAAAnd..... she did nothing else. No character development, no nothing, nada. Almost as if she was a nothing. <br /><br />I have to say that this plot line also dragged a bit. Some moments I found myself rereading the same line over and over and over and over and over, just because I was falling asleep, because of the nothingness happening. Compared to the first novel in the franchise, <b>this is an ant compared to a mountain.</b> I expected a little, sorry, a LOT more from the author in this novel.<br /><br />This was a good book to read. It pulled me up out of my book hangover after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23766634.A_Court_of_Wings_and_Ruin__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___3_" title="A Court of Wings and Ruin (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #3) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Wings and Ruin</a>, but <b>it had a long way to match its predecessor.</b><br /><br />-------------------------<br /><u>
  <i>Books in Series</i>
</u>:<br />#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1962162621" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prisoner of Cell 25</a>: ★★★.75<br />#2 Rise of the Elgen: ★★★</span>
  <a data-text-id="6899566285296560908" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4318278322282214058" style="display:none">First read: November 11-18, 2012<br />Re-read: September 12-16, 2016<br /><br />My feelings for the series, so far, have remained the same; though there is a flaw or two, I can look past that and still enjoy the series. It still makes my heart race faster and my ears hot with every one of Hatch's sermons. And the rats.<br /><br />Speaking of rats, this book gets a little darker than its predecessor. Since rats have become such a common phobia, with good understanding, they are used as not only the source of the main plot device, but as a physical and a psychological torture device.<br /><br />Also, this sequel acts as a bulk for more character development, which is why there are some slow parts here and there and much more than the first book had, which was more about action and adventure. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353844478" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1046228-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603694939p2/1046228.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/1046228-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353844478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18227120698905666130">I liked this book, BUT, please note, don't read this book right before you are going to eat. There are some icky descriptions that totally grossed me out and made me loose my appetite! They did pertain to the story and plot and actually developed it, but it was still really gross and they are throughout the entire book. ewe. With that said, this is a 4½ star book for me. <br/><br/>I liked how the characters are developing and how they work together. The plot was also good. It's sorta like a Jame's Bond mo</span>
  <span id="freeText18227120698905666130" style="display:none">I liked this book, BUT, please note, don't read this book right before you are going to eat. There are some icky descriptions that totally grossed me out and made me loose my appetite! They did pertain to the story and plot and actually developed it, but it was still really gross and they are throughout the entire book. ewe. With that said, this is a 4½ star book for me. <br /><br />I liked how the characters are developing and how they work together. The plot was also good. It's sorta like a Jame's Bond movie with teenagers starring in it. <br /><br />They really need to make a movie out of this book! I've heard that many have been inquiring about the rights to this series from the author...<br /><br />Also, it will be difficult to wait a ::whole:: year to hear what happens next. Richard Paul Evans, please write even faster than you already are! A whole year is faaaarrrrr too long to wait!<br /><br />I have tons of other thoughts, but they contain spoilers and are mentioned below if you scroll. If you haven't read this, please skip these spoilers.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />For spoilers, please scroll below:<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Okay, I loved this book, but I have a few questions:<br /><br />1. Once the main group (minus Michael) escapes the compound in Peru, how come Elgen didn't send out any guards to chase them in the jungle? I mean, the Elgen really would love to get their hands on all those people and have a serious interest in punishing them all for various reasons, it seemed weird that the Electroclan could just rest right by the pipe they escaped from. They sure had no problem sending 1,000+ guards out into the jungle to try and capture Michael when he escaped...<br /><br /><br />2. I would have liked to have seen more about Michael's magnetic powers. I don't feel like he was able to develop them very well and wondered how he made himself stick and unstick with the magnetism, which was huge in saving him since it bought him some valuable time when he was being lowered into the bowl (along with his friends sabatoging the water on the compound that effected the cooling). His powers just did what he needed them to and I had the feeling he truly had not fully understood them or perfected them.<br /><br />3. I ::hate:: rats. They are so gross, so this really grossed me out in the book. So, how did they get the rats from the bowl to the hallway where the Electroclan were at? AND, how was Elgen planning on getting the hoards of rats back into the bowl after they attacked the Electroclan? Since the Elgen assumed the rats would prevail, they must have had a plan to get them back into the bowl - unless it was a emotional decision Hatch made out of desperation to beat Michael so badly. It was interesting to me that Hatch would take the risk of having the rats take over the entire plant for not having a way to harness them and get them back to their caged bowl. I guess psycho villains sometimes make emotional decisions in the heat of the moment when they are threatened or experiencing the fear of being compromised...<br /><br />4. How the heck did they clean up all the fried rats? awk! AND how were there ::that:: many rats to still be in the bowl after the whole sprinkler incident in the hallway? Supposedly they had one million rats, but still, that had to have taken out a few hundred thousand rats for the hallway incident. ewe, gross. I can't even begin to imagine the smells... so gross. I'm assuming that they didn't clean up the fried rats, since the whole compound was going down, they probably abandoned it. It still grosses me out thinking about it.<br /><br />Now for predictions/thoughts for the next book in the series:<br /><br />I think the Amazon tribesmen will let Michael go. I don't think he will dwell with them forever in the jungle. I think they are just helping him, and if they want to keep him, he will still get away. I think he will be reunited with the Electroclan in book 3, but I think it may take a minute for him to get out of there. I also wonder if the Electroclan really got to their escape helicopters... we never heard a helicopter other than the four Elgen helicopters that were brought down. Hopefully the group is waiting for Michael and I would expect that Ian can see him and tell what is happening, so they can rescue him. Ostin prolly speaks Amazon tibestalk... <br /><br />Hatch was more psycho/evil than ever, and I suspect he won't be caught by Michael for a long time - to keep the series going. What good is this series without a proper antagonist? I'm very curious to see what backlash the Board has for Hatch after having the Peru plant melt down due to Michael and his friends. I also wonder how successful Hatch will be when his unlimited supply of money runs out from his only source, the Board. Will the evil Electric kids still want to stick with him, even if he has no money since the Board will clearly not be backing him anymore? Money seems to have been the main motivation of the evil electric kids to stay with Hatch. They might stick with him, since he's such a wack-job with his mind control he has over them. It will be very interesting to see if the Board gets Hatch and has can discipline/kill him for what he has done... Obviously the Board will be seeking Hatch in the future books... <br /><br />I'm hoping that the Electroclan will be able to meet the people behind "the Voice" after what they did to help them in this book (destroying the biggest plant the Elgen has, and discrediting them but ruining their newest business venture of cheap, rat power) - I think the Electroclan deserve to meet these people, especially since they aided their cause big time by bringing down Elgen. I'm very curious to see who this secret organization is and how they are funded. They apparently have an endless supply of money like the Elgen do. I also hope that the people behind "the Voice" get the Electroclan's families out of Meridian, ID and into some sort of witness protection program. Otherwise, I can see this series having the same plot over and over of trying to rescue various family members of the Electroclan. <br /><br />I think there is a possibility that the Electroclan will become spies for "the Voice" and that they will be on a never-ending battle to catch Hatch and the evil Electric kids. I also think there is a strong possibility that Hatch will find another evil, villian organization to work for that will help him try to gain his goal of world power and dodge the wrath of the Board that he had worked for 20+ years, especially since the Board will want to totally kill him.<br /><br />Last of all, I seem to vaguely remember it was mentioned that other Electric children exist in the world besides the kids created from the machine from Elgen in California. It will be very interesting to see their role in future books.<br /><br />Awesome series! </span>
  <a data-text-id="18227120698905666130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8086235001443116947" style="display:none"> Michael Vey and his electric friends (aka the Electroclan) have escaped from the Elgen's capture but they are still being hunted down. Michael’s powers amplified throughout the book. His leadership skills grew immensely when they were facing everything, from explosions and electric rats to missing family members and life-threatening missions.<br /><br /> When the adventure starts, Michael and his ragtag group of friends are trying to hide in their small home town in Idaho. They are attempting to regroup and to download and investigate the information that one of the electric kids had downloaded from the Elgen’s compound. The Elgen guards are waiting for them in their town and are attempting to recapture them. They end up in a tanning place and Michael is given an a mysterious cell phone from a random lady. It can only be activated by electric people, and when Michael answered the phone, a voice tells him he wants to help the kids.<br /> The Electroclan have learned to trust no one and to create their own plan. One of the many dangers the Electroclan got into was a high speed car chase with the Elgen that lead to an explosion. They end up in Peru with help from the mysterious man on the phone.<br /><br /> While all of that is going on, Hatch is preparing and organizing his army, led by the electric children that idolize him. The Elgen still have Michael’s mother and they are building a race of electricity-creating super-rats, and are training Elgen guards from all over the world for Hatch’s world domination plan.<br /><br /> Michael and the Electroclan make their way into the Elgen compound for the rescue. They are get recaptured, and the scenes with the rats will keep readers turning pages quickly to find out how they escape. But one member of the Electroclan must stay and face Hatch to let the others escape, and Michael steps in. Hatch has let his issues with Michael become very personal and devises a particularly horrible torture and death for him. But everyone has underestimated Michael’s powers, both electric and otherwise.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15572938213844890450">What I love about this book is how the author adds a lot of detail to picture the setting and what the characters look like. I also love this book because of the way the author expresses what the characters feel and it definitely adds a lot of details. What I also love about this book is that the author adds a lot of suspense and keeps all the audience on the edge of their seats. I love that this book is a series and throughout every book the plot thickens. I also love this book because it defin</span>
  <span id="freeText15572938213844890450" style="display:none">What I love about this book is how the author adds a lot of detail to picture the setting and what the characters look like. I also love this book because of the way the author expresses what the characters feel and it definitely adds a lot of details. What I also love about this book is that the author adds a lot of suspense and keeps all the audience on the edge of their seats. I love that this book is a series and throughout every book the plot thickens. I also love this book because it definitely feels as though you are actually there with the characters.<br /><br />Some things I didn't like was how the author did not specifically talk about the background story of what happens if there happens to be a reader who just picks up one of these books thats in the middle of the series. I also don't like how the author explains a little more on what happens to certain characters. I also don't like how the author leave out characters that were in the series. I don't like how the author does not mention whether or not if it was the next day or if it's the same day. I also don't like how the author does not add a lot of detail to new locations that the characters are taken to.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to readers who love action. I would also recommend this book to readers who love suspence and being on the edge of their seats. I would not recommend readers to this book if there just going to take the book that's in the middle of the series. I would also recommend this book to readers who really love to see what characters feel during a certain time in the book. I would also recommend this book to people who love details and want to feel like they are actually in the book.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2270325931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9478204713335667712">Good enough, for what it is - commercial fiction aimed at youngsters in the early- to mid-teens. The flaws don't really hinder its intended purpose, which is to be entertaining enough to keep you turning one more page - and maybe even pick up the next book in the series once you've been hooked in. The textual equivalent of a summertime Hollywood special-effects action flick; characters will occasionally turn to the camera at the dramatic moment and say something cheesy that no actual person woul</span>
  <span id="freeText9478204713335667712" style="display:none">Good enough, for what it is - commercial fiction aimed at youngsters in the early- to mid-teens. The flaws don't really hinder its intended purpose, which is to be entertaining enough to keep you turning one more page - and maybe even pick up the next book in the series once you've been hooked in. The textual equivalent of a summertime Hollywood special-effects action flick; characters will occasionally turn to the camera at the dramatic moment and say something cheesy that no actual person would say under such circumstances, but that the producers thought "sounded cool." As long as you suspend disbelief and don't press the film's logic too hard, everything comes out all right. <br /><br />One bone I do have to pick: at one point the main character uses his power to hurt a "bad guy" in a purely vengeful way, out of anger. None of his friends or any other "good guy" denounces this act, the book doesn't sanction it in any way or acknowledge that this is a step in the road to becoming a "bad guy". Not ok. The teens in general are pretty quick to use their powers in violent ways to harm "bad guys" as they go about trying to save the world. Something to have a conversation about, if you're going to let your offspring read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9478204713335667712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2008010485" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2008010485" />
    <a title="Alex Reynolds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58987235-alex-reynolds"><img alt="Alex Reynolds" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2008010485?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex Reynolds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex Reynolds" href="/user/show/58987235-alex-reynolds">Alex Reynolds</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2008010485&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2008010485" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6873449886454470165">This bok is fast paced and action packed. The author Richard Paul Evans does a good job in not dragging stuff out too far but just enough. The main character is cool but my favorite is Zeus a round character who started out bad and became good. He is really powerful but cant shower so is made fun of for smells (he cant shower without hurting himself.) The end of the book is great because, Michael Vey takes the energy from electric rats and then vaporizes them.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1532473638237150815">This second installment is actually better than the first; it's rather ingenious to have the Elgen use the electrified rats as an efficient power source to take over the world through the economy. Better than Hatch's plan to take the world by force.<br/><br/>Wait, that's still his plan? And that's his plan for ALL SEVEN BOOKS?<br/><br/><i>*virtual facepalm*</i><br/><br/>Yeah, nevermind. It's kinda entertaining though. When you can look past the clichés and absurdities. And when you're twelve years old.<br/><br/>*Side note: I realized when re</span>
  <span id="freeText1532473638237150815" style="display:none">This second installment is actually better than the first; it's rather ingenious to have the Elgen use the electrified rats as an efficient power source to take over the world through the economy. Better than Hatch's plan to take the world by force.<br /><br />Wait, that's still his plan? And that's his plan for ALL SEVEN BOOKS?<br /><br /><i>*virtual facepalm*</i><br /><br />Yeah, nevermind. It's kinda entertaining though. When you can look past the clichés and absurdities. And when you're twelve years old.<br /><br />*Side note: I realized when re-reading this that Hatch's "eagles and chickens" philosophy bears more than a marginal resemblance to that of Nietzsche, possibly cross-bred with a bit of Machiavelli. Not sure if that was the intention, but it was an interesting (although rather obvious) discovery nonetheless.</span>

I have been listening to this in my car as I drive to and from work. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cAkGKEQVkDcklcLvTWC3s2Wgr6vn4Ej4dKWGo5n3Cjn+nFtnjbLO1Aj+k6lv7d8Qd0M4zftsWwWnPyXmZf1Ljw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ValqRz0YrwM8UAgk3kJtY1FIHCvvrjyn58Y0iIS0DkzbPDcI9L/x4BA7WWL8zwXAQ6uLTfMiL1o0XJfNeL5P+g==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16598550948188948035">When Richard Paul Evans wrote the #1 best-seller, The Christmas Box, he never intended on becoming an internationally known author. His quiet story of parental love and the true meaning of Christmas made history when it became simultaneously the #1 hardcover and paperback book in the nation. Since then, more than eight million copies of The Christmas Box have been printed. He has since written ele</span>
  <span id="freeText16598550948188948035" style="display:none">When Richard Paul Evans wrote the #1 best-seller, The Christmas Box, he never intended on becoming an internationally known author. His quiet story of parental love and the true meaning of Christmas made history when it became simultaneously the #1 hardcover and paperback book in the nation. Since then, more than eight million copies of The Christmas Box have been printed. He has since written eleven consecutive New York Times bestsellers. He is one the few authors in history to have hit both the fiction and non-fiction bestseller lists. He has won several awards for his books including the 1998 American Mothers Book Award, two first place Storytelling World Awards, and the 2005 Romantic Times Best Women Novel of the Year Award. His books have been translated into more than 22 languages and several have been international best sellers.</span>
